- **Document-detail mobile (locked 2026-04-26):** the [/documents/[id]](<src/app/(platform)/documents/[id]/page.tsx>) main grid (`gridTemplateColumns: '1fr 380px'`) and the tab bar (`flex-wrap + overflow:hidden`) BOTH had no mobile breakpoint. On phones the sidebar column crushed the main content and the tab bar silently clipped the second row of tabs. Fix shipped 2026-04-26: classes `doc-detail-main-grid` + `doc-detail-tab-bar` plus a scoped `<style>` block at the bottom of the page with a `@media (max-width: 900px)` rule that stacks the grid to a single column and switches the tab bar to horizontal scroll. **Don't add new top-level inline styles** that override these classes on the same elements without also adding a matching mobile override; the `<style>` block is the single mobile override and has to win on the narrow viewport.

- **Education Room — flashcard + recall + apply mastery engine (locked 2026-04-28):** [EducationRoomTab](src/components/founder-hub/EducationRoomTab.tsx) is the founder-hub's recollection engine. Reading Closing Lab + Sales Toolkit + founder-context builds familiarity; recollection under pressure builds the muscle that fires in a live conversation. **Three modes per deck**: Flashcard (passive recall — see prompt, click to flip, self-grade missed/almost/got-it; SM-2 spaced repetition tracks card mastery over time), Recall (active recall — type the answer in your own voice, gemini-3.1-flash-lite grades semantically against canonical, returns score 0-100 + grade letter + what landed + what missed + coach note + canonical reveal), Apply (scenario application drill — see prompt + a concrete scenario context like "you're on a procurement call with a GC", type how you'd USE the concept, AI grades application quality). **SSOT** at [education-room-data.ts](src/components/founder-hub/education/education-room-data.ts) — 15 decks × 161 cards as of 2026-05-02 (was 12 decks × ~100 at the 2026-04-28 lock; expanded with `advanced_sales_moves`, `strategic_thinking`, `goldner_discovery` decks per the Brinkmanship + Strategic Thinking + Goldner Discovery additions): DI Vocabulary (20 cards — locked + banned + cold-context bridges + numbers like 135 decisions / 17 frameworks / ~90% margin / per-audit cost / specimen library / first design partner Sankore-marked-confidential), Buyer Personas (14 cards — basics + verbatim opener + canonical objection-handler response per persona), Maalouf 6 Principles, Satyam 5 Pillars, Silent Objections (5 — each with current ship status: shipped / in-progress / todo so the founder always sees the gap), Sales DQI Rubric (11 dimensions — one card per dimension with excellent/poor + weight), Cognitive Biases (10 most common in strategic memos — confirmation, anchoring, sunk-cost, narrative fallacy, overconfidence, availability, halo effect, illusion of control, planning fallacy, loss aversion as both bias-to-defend AND sales-tool), 12-Node Pipeline (6 representative — structuralAssumptions, biasDetective, noiseJudge, rpdRecognition, pre-mortem, metaJudge), DQI Methodology (5 — components+weights, grade boundaries 85/70/55/40, Brier score, recalibration, validation), 17 Regulatory Frameworks (8 most invoked — EU AI Act Art 14, Basel III ICAAP, GDPR Art 22, NDPR, CBN, WAEMU, PoPIA s.71, ISA 2007 with current TODO-gap callout), R²F Framework (5 — Kahneman side / Klein side / metaJudge arbitration / 2009 anchor paper / competitor gap), Founder One-Liners (8 — External Attack Vectors, ICP wedge vs ceiling, generic-VC-segment-to-avoid, primary one-liner, secondary regulatory variant, protected-revenue framing, outcome-gate strategic purpose, design-partner contractual asks). **Each card** carries: stable id slug (used as localStorage key for SM-2 state), prompt, canonicalAnswer (ground truth for AI grading), optional hint, difficulty (foundation/core/advanced), applicationContext (when this comes up in real conversation — used as apply-mode scenario), source citation, optional category tag. **SM-2 spaced repetition lite** in `applySm2()` helper — tracks easeFactor / repetitions / intervalDays / lastReviewed / nextDue / totalReviews / successfulReviews per card; cards graded "missed" come up sooner, "got it" cards push out exponentially. Deck picker shows per-deck mastery (% of cards with ≥2 successful reviews) + due-card count. **API endpoint**: [/api/founder-hub/education/grade-recall](src/app/api/founder-hub/education/grade-recall/route.ts) uses gemini-3.1-flash-lite (cheap, classification-grade) at temperature 0.3 for recall grading consistency; mock fallback when GOOGLE_API_KEY missing. Founder-pass auth. **Persistence**: localStorage `di-education-room-sm2-v1` (per-card SM-2 state), `di-education-room-session-v1` (lifetime reviewed/got-it/almost/missed counts). **Per-card recall cost**: ~£0.005-0.015 (one cheap Gemini call per recall submission). **When to use**: morning before a London networking event (drill the persona-opener deck for whoever you'll meet), after every CLAUDE.md positioning lock change (the relevant cards inherit the new vocab — re-drill them), before any procurement-stage call (drill the regulatory-frameworks deck). Tab id `education_room` registered in Go-to-Market group between Closing Lab and Sparring Room — the read→recall→do flow. **Forward-looking rule**: when CLAUDE.md positioning vocabulary changes, update the relevant card.canonicalAnswer in education-room-data.ts in the same commit. When a new persona / framework / lesson lands, add a card. The founder is the only consumer; cards are written in HIS voice for HIS recall — not generic SaaS marketing copy. Pattern lifted from [Nexus Tracker](https://github.com/FolahanWilliams/nexus-tracker) MindForge (vocab + summary + impromptu-speaking modules with SM-2 spaced repetition), extended for DI's specific knowledge surface.
- **Brinkmanship + Strategic Thinking (locked 2026-04-28 PM):** Two new sections in [SalesToolkitTab](src/components/founder-hub/SalesToolkitTab.tsx) sourcing from Schelling "The Strategy of Conflict" (1960) + Dixit & Nalebuff "Thinking Strategically" (1991). **Brinkmanship section** — 4 game-theory moves that flip the power dynamic by deliberately creating the risk of a mutually-bad outcome (the deal dying): Evidence-Moment ultimatum · weaponized honest off-ramp · reject the unpaid dev shop · natural scarcity on pilot seats. Each carries verbatim phrase + mechanism + anti-pattern + which Sparring dimension it scores against + best-for-persona. Stored as `BRINKMANSHIP_MOVES: SalesMove[]` in [sales-toolkit.ts](src/lib/data/sales-toolkit.ts). **Strategic Thinking Principles** — 5 higher-order positioning anchors that govern HOW DI is built, sold, and positioned (look-forward-reason-backward, strategic moves by limiting options, credible commitments, setting category ground rules, cooperation/coordination over competition). Stored as `STRATEGIC_THINKING_PRINCIPLES: StrategicPrinciple[]` with `principle / summary / diApplication / whenItBites` fields. Rendered via new `StrategicPrinciplesList` component at the bottom of SalesToolkitTab. **Education Room extensions**: 4 brinkmanship cards added to `advanced_sales_moves` deck + new `strategic_thinking` deck (5 cards × principles). **Sparring grade prompt awareness**: brinkmanship is now named as the META-PATTERN that fires when `mutual_disqualification + pressure_without_pressure + damaging_admission` cluster high (4-5) together. The grader is instructed to call it out in the strengths array as "brinkmanship signal · power dynamic flipped" with the specific transcript phrase, and to flag the inverse (founder agreeing to every feature request, hedging, chasing the deal) as a recurring pattern when it shows in `recentDimensionAverages`. **Why brinkmanship is NOT a 16th dimension**: it's the meta-pattern that emerges from existing dimensions clustering — adding it as its own dimension would double-count. Treating it as a meta-signal preserves the rubric's parsimony while still surfacing the highest-leverage sales psychology move. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding new sales-toolkit moves, treat the existing 15 dimensions as the canonical grading surface; if a new "framework" doesn't decompose into those, don't add it as a dimension — surface it as a SalesMove and let it score against existing dimensions. The grade prompt should be the only place where meta-patterns (like brinkmanship) are named.
- **EducationRoomTab purity + static-component fixes (locked 2026-04-28 PM):** Two ESLint react-hooks rules were tripping CI on the Education Room: (a) `react-hooks/purity` flagged `Date.now()` inside the `deckMastery` useMemo (computing due-card counts) — fix: hoist to a `useState(() => Date.now())` mountTime, capture once, depend the useMemo on the captured value. Minute-level precision is enough for due-card counting; we don't refresh as the user sits on the page. (b) `react-hooks/static-components` flagged the `const Icon = getIcon(...)` pattern in DeckPicker + CardHeader because the resolved component reference would change shape on each render. Fix: declare a module-scoped `<DeckIcon name=... size=... style=... />` component that handles the lookup internally; both call sites now render `<DeckIcon ... />` instead of resolving an icon-component reference inline. Pattern: any `getIcon`-style helper that returns a component constructor needs to be wrapped in a module-scope component to satisfy the static-components rule.
- **Sparring Room v3 (locked 2026-04-28 PM — coach-not-judge upgrade + 4 new dimensions + DQI uptrend visualisation):** Major iteration on the original Sparring Room. (1) **15-dimension rubric** — added `fomu_calibration` (JOLT Effect / Matt Dixon), `damaging_admission` (Cialdini + Cohen Naked Business), `mutual_disqualification` (Sandler), `prescriptive_recommendation` (JOLT) per NotebookLM synthesis on "what failure modes is the rubric NOT catching" (KB note 0cc18c5d). Weights rebalanced to sum to 1.0 across 15 dims. (2) **Coach-not-judge result schema** — every grading response now includes `nextSessionFocus` (2-3 dimensions to laser on next rep, with whyItMatters + concreteAction), `drillPlan` (2-4 ordered concrete actions before next rep, each pointing at a specific Founder Hub surface like "Education Room → Buyer Personas deck → Adaeze cards" with estimatedMinutes), `confidenceBuild` (1-2 sentences naming what GENUINELY worked — not generic praise), `nextRepSetup` (recommendedPersonaId + recommendedMode + rationale based on this rep's score: ≥80 = harder, 60-79 = same persona × different mode, <60 = same persona × easier mode), and conditionally `patternFlag` (only fires at 3+ reps when a recurring weakness shows in `recentDimensionAverages` — pattern + rootCause + breakthroughMove). The grade route now accepts `recentDimensionAverages` (last-5 rolling per-dimension averages from history) + `totalRepsCompleted` and feeds them to the prompt for longitudinal coaching. (3) **DQI uptrend viz** — new [SparringTrendViz](src/components/founder-hub/sparring/SparringTrendViz.tsx) component renders 3 panels: line chart (DQI per rep + 5-rep rolling average + grade-band markers + best-rep callout), per-dimension trend bars (sorted by lift first-5-vs-last-5, source-color coded), and persona×mode performance heatmap (avg DQI per cell with rep count). Pure SVG, respects prefers-reduced-motion. (4) **HistoryEntry shape extended** to v2 capturing `dimensions: Record<GradingDimensionId, number>` + `fillerCount` per rep so the viz has real data; v1 entries (no dimensions) still load gracefully. **Original Sparring Room features preserved**: 7 buyer personas, 7 scenario modes (incl. networking-event-in-person), Wispr Flow paste-transcript flow, mock fallback. **Pattern detection unlocks at 3+ reps** to avoid noisy single-rep flagging. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding a new grading dimension, update GRADING_DIMENSIONS array + GradingDimensionId union + grade prompt's dimensions block + grade prompt's required JSON output template + mock fallback dims object — all in same commit. The weights MUST sum to 1.0 (verify by hand; runtime panic disabled). The earlier 2026-04-28 lock (networking-event mode + Kahneman loss-aversion) stays — this v3 entry supersedes the prior coverage of result-schema + UI sections.
- **Sparring Room — live sales-rep practice (locked 2026-04-28, SUPERSEDED by Sparring Room v3 entry above which lifted the rubric to 15 dimensions; this v1 entry retained for historical context only):** [SparringRoomTab](src/components/founder-hub/SparringRoomTab.tsx) is the founder-hub's reading→doing transition. Closing Lab gives the verbatim phrases per persona; Sparring Room makes you LIVE them under pressure. Workflow: pick buyer persona × scenario mode → AI generates 3 buyer-voice questions in their authentic voice + an opener line → 5-second prep countdown → user records voice answer via Wispr Flow externally (NO in-app transcription — Wispr Flow handles voice→text system-wide) → pastes transcript → AI grades on an 11-dimension Sales DQI rubric (Maalouf 4 + Satyam 3 + DI discipline 2 + Kahneman 1 loss-aversion-framing + fundamentals 1) → returns score + 2 strengths + 3 framework-grounded improvements with verbatim phrases the founder can rehearse + a buyer-perspective simulation showing what the buyer is internally thinking right after the speech. **Architecture**: SSOT at [sparring-room-data.ts](src/components/founder-hub/sparring/sparring-room-data.ts) — 7 buyer personas (Adaeze mid-market PE / Potomac boutique sell-side M&A / Marcus solo fractional CSO + Margaret F500 CSO / Titi Pan-African fund partner / James GC + Riya pre-seed VC), **7 scenario modes** including the new `networking_event_inperson` mode (London networking events — 30-60 second connect-not-pitch with the buyer holding a drink, pre-loaded scenario templates for Margaret-class CSO / Potomac-class M&A head / Titi-class fund partner / Marcus-class fractional CSO / Riya-class VC associate at networking mixers), 11 grading dimensions with explicit excellent/poor descriptions + weights summing to 1.0, 27 scenario templates pairing personas with modes for AI generation hints, plus mechanical analysis utilities. **Loss-aversion framing dimension (Kahneman source, weight 0.10)**: grounded in Kahneman & Tversky 1979 prospect theory — losses weight ~2-2.5× gains in decision-making. Excellent: frames value as preventing a SPECIFIC, named loss the buyer is already worrying about (regrettable strategic mistake, McKinsey bill, LP pulling capital), anchored against a comparable cost. Poor: frames as upside / gain only ('better decisions', 'improved quality') — buyer hears upside and discounts. Weights rebalanced when adding loss-aversion: Maalouf reduced from 4×0.10 to 0.08/0.10/0.10/0.08; Satyam reduced 0.10/0.12/0.08 to 0.08/0.10/0.08; DI discipline reduced vocabulary 0.08→0.06; specificity stays 0.12; new Kahneman 0.10. Sum = 1.00. **Two API endpoints**: [/api/founder-hub/sparring/generate-questions](src/app/api/founder-hub/sparring/generate-questions/route.ts) uses gemini-3-flash-preview at temperature 0.7 to generate persona-voice opener + 3 questions, mock fallback when GOOGLE_API_KEY missing; [/api/founder-hub/sparring/grade](src/app/api/founder-hub/sparring/grade/route.ts) uses gemini-3-flash-preview at temperature 0.4 (lower for grading consistency) returning the full SparringSessionResult schema, plus mechanical filler/banned/locked vocabulary detection that runs WITHOUT calling Gemini. Founder-pass auth on both. **Vocabulary discipline awareness**: the `vocabulary_discipline` dimension downgrades use of locked DI vocabulary (reasoning layer / R²F / DPR / DQI) on COLD-context buyers — the founder picks isWarmContext per session, defaulting to false. The `empathic_mode_first` dimension grades whether the founder led with the BUYER's pain in BUYER's vocabulary BEFORE introducing product. Banned-vocabulary list (decision intelligence platform / decision hygiene / boardroom strategic decision / etc.) auto-detected and surfaced as explicit hit count on results. **Persistence**: localStorage `di-sparring-room-history-v1` tracks recent reps with sales DQI trend (last 5 reps delta + average + per-rep grade letters). **Per-rep cost**: ~£0.05-0.10 (one Gemini call for question generation + one for grading). Heavy use ~3-5 reps/day per session. **When to use**: before any high-stakes meeting (rehearse the persona you're calling), after every lost deal (replay the conversation against the buyer who actually killed it), as muscle-memory training for the Maalouf "authority not trust" + Satyam "conviction transmission" dimensions. Tab id `sparring_room` registered in Go-to-Market group between Closing Lab and Outreach Hub. **Forward-looking rule**: when a new buyer persona archetype emerges from real meetings, add to BUYER_PERSONAS in sparring-room-data.ts in the same commit as any persona-related copy elsewhere (CLAUDE.md ICP, founder-context.ts, role-empty-states). When CLAUDE.md banned/locked vocabulary changes, update DI_BANNED_VOCABULARY and DI_LOCKED_VOCABULARY in sparring-room-data.ts in the same commit. Pattern lifted from [Nexus Tracker](https://github.com/FolahanWilliams/nexus-tracker) MindForge impromptu-speaking module, extended for B2B sales conversations.

- **DPR v2 enhancements (locked 2026-04-26 — schema bumped to v2, six new sections from NotebookLM "highest-ROI DPR additions" synthesis):** the Decision Provenance Record generator at [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts) now ships six new procurement-grade blocks alongside the existing 4-page core. Page sequence: (1) cover with Integrity Fingerprints + new **Verification block** (re-verification path, "tamper-evident today, private-key signing on Q3 2026 roadmap" honesty) + new **Org Calibration strip** (Cloverpop defense — proves the DQI is calibrated against THIS org's outcome history, not a generic benchmark) + new **Counterfactual Impact block** (top-3 bias scenarios with expected improvement %, sample-size + Wilson confidence, monetary anchor when DecisionFrame.value is present), (2) model lineage + judge variance, (3) academic citations + 17-framework regulatory mapping, (4) pipeline lineage + appendix, (5) NEW **Reviewer Decisions / HITL log** (accepted mitigations, dismissed flags with reasons, dissent log, final sign-off — EU AI Act Art 14 + Basel III Pillar 2 ICAAP qualitative-decision documentation; only rendered when reviewerDecisions.reviewedAt is non-null), (6) blind-prior aggregations (when present), (7) Decision Package or Deal members (when applicable), (8) NEW **Data Lifecycle footer** ALWAYS as the last page (retention window per plan tier, encryption posture, sub-processors, right-to-erasure, production region, published roadmap items — the procurement-grade contractual statement F500 vendor-risk registers ask for in writing). New top-level field: **Client-Safe Export Mode** (`generate(data, { clientSafe: true })`) — entity names, amounts, and person names in the meta strip + summary + reviewer notes are replaced with stable `[ENTITY_N]` / `[AMOUNT_N]` / `[NAME_N]` placeholders so the artefact can be shared with an LP, regulator, or third-party assurance firm without leaking competitive intelligence. Wired through three API routes via `?clientSafe=1` query param: [/api/documents/[id]/provenance-record](src/app/api/documents/[id]/provenance-record/route.ts), [/api/decision-packages/[id]/provenance-record](src/app/api/decision-packages/[id]/provenance-record/route.ts), [/api/deals/[id]/provenance-record](src/app/api/deals/[id]/provenance-record/route.ts), and the public specimen at [/api/public/sample-dpr](src/app/api/public/sample-dpr/route.ts). The assembler at [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) populates counterfactualImpact (via `computeCounterfactuals(analysisId, orgId)`), orgCalibration (via `getOrgBrierStats(prisma, orgId)` + `Analysis.recalibratedDqi`), and dataLifecycle (always populated, pulls plan-tier retention + sub-processor list + roadmap) — each block is independently fault-tolerant; failure to populate one returns undefined and the PDF skips that section honestly rather than fabricating data. reviewerDecisions stays undefined in the live assembler until the capture UI ships; the SPECIMEN at [sample-dpr.ts](src/lib/reports/sample-dpr.ts) seeds plausible v2 values across all six new sections so a CSO + GC can preview the full v2 shape via `/api/public/sample-dpr?clientSafe=0|1` before signing anything. **Vocabulary discipline**: the cover purpose strap reads "Hashed and tamper-evident evidence record..." — the prior overclaim "signed, hashed" is gone; restore "signed" only when private-key signing actually ships per `trust-copy.ts` lock. **The strategic point**: this DPR v2 is the leave-behind artefact that lands the warm-intro meeting (LRQA / Ian Spaulding, Sankore, future F500 conversations) — it carries (a) Cloverpop-defense (org calibration), (b) IBM-watsonx-defense (HITL log proving humans governed the call), (c) agentic-shift-defense (the artefact maps onto ANY structured decision artefact, not just human-authored memos), and (d) procurement-grade transparency that LRQA-style assurance firms recognise as their own vocabulary.
- **Kahneman & Klein 2009 paper-application sprint EXTENDED (locked 2026-04-30 — items 6 of 10):** Second batch ships #8 / #2-structural / #9 alongside the first batch's #5 / #3 / #6. The DPR cover page now carries SIX procurement-grade Kahneman-Klein-anchored signals in addition to the existing audit summary: **Validity classification → Org Calibration → Feedback Adequacy → Reference Class Forecast → Counterfactual Impact → Recommended Action**. **(#8 — Reference Class Forecasting · Kahneman & Lovallo 2003 "Delusions of Success" HBR)** New module [reference-class-forecast.ts](src/lib/learning/reference-class-forecast.ts) — pure-function similarity scoring against the 143-case library (no LLM call, deterministic, <5ms). Returns top-5 historical analogs + matched-class baseline failure rate + four-band predicted outcome (succeeds / mixed / struggles / fails / too_small_to_judge). Wired into [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts); rendered as a colour-coded REFERENCE CLASS FORECAST · {BAND} strip on every DPR cover. Specimen seeded with WeWork (2019) as the lead analog. Cold-start posture is honest — structurally novel decisions return `reference_class_too_small_to_judge` rather than a fabricated forecast. **(#2 — Validity Classifier with structural DQI shift · Kahneman & Klein 2009 first condition)** New module [validity-classifier.ts](src/lib/learning/validity-classifier.ts) — `classifyValidity({ documentType, industry, decisionHorizon? })` returns one of four bands (high / medium / low / zero) with a rationale string. `getValidityWeightShift(class)` returns `Partial<WEIGHTS>` deltas applied via [computeEffectiveWeights](src/lib/scoring/dqi.ts) — in low-validity environments: `+0.10 historicalAlignment, +0.02 biasLoad, −0.05 evidenceQuality, −0.04 processMaturity, −0.03 complianceRisk` (re-normalised to sum 1.0). In zero-validity: `+0.20 historicalAlignment, +0.04 biasLoad, −0.08 evidenceQuality, −0.10 processMaturity, −0.06 complianceRisk`. **METHODOLOGY_VERSION bumped 2.0.0 → 2.1.0** (locked 2026-04-30); legacy inputs without `validityClass` still report `'2.0.0-no-validity'` so a procurement reader can tell which methodology produced a given DQI. Wired into all 3 DQI computation paths: [/api/dqi](src/app/api/dqi/route.ts), [/api/v1/dqi](src/app/api/v1/dqi/route.ts), [/api/explainability/[id]](src/app/api/explainability/[analysisId]/route.ts). DPR renders a VALIDITY · {BAND} strip with rationale + methodology version. **(#9 — Inside-View Dominance · DI-B-022 · Kahneman & Lovallo 2003)** New bias entry — the 22nd in the stable taxonomy. Cascade: BiasCategory union + BIAS_CATEGORIES, [bias-education.ts](src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts) DI-B-022 entry with the 1976 Israeli curriculum-writing team as the canonical example, [bias-normalize.ts](src/lib/utils/bias-normalize.ts) ALIASES ("Inside-View Dominance" / "reference class neglect" / "outside view neglect"), [BIAS_DETECTIVE_PROMPT](src/lib/agents/prompts.ts) taxonomy item #22 detecting "this case is special" / "the comparables don't apply" / projections without grounded comparables, four new compound interactions (+ Planning Fallacy 1.6×, + Overconfidence 1.5×, + Illusion of Validity 1.4×, + Confirmation 1.3×), new toxic combination "Reference-Class Blindness" (Inside-View + Planning Fallacy + Overconfidence — the canonical Kahneman & Lovallo failure pattern). `forgottenQuestions` taxonomy enum lifted 32 → 33. **Education Room** gained four new flashcards (`bias_reference_class_forecasting`, `bias_validity_classifier`, `bias_inside_view_dominance`, plus the three from batch one) — kahneman_klein tag, advanced tier. **Why this matters**: R²F was previously claimed in marketing copy but only partially operationalised. Six DPR cover blocks anchored in Kahneman-Klein-Lovallo papers, with academic citations + DOI references in every bias-education entry, makes the moat citable not just claimable. The next 4 paper applications (`#1` Fractionation of Expertise, `#10` Calibrated Rejection of Subjective Confidence, `#7` Algorithm-aversion Counter-programming, `#4` Improper Linear Models / Decision Rubric) are the remaining ranked queue. **Forward-looking rule**: every new R²F detector lands with academic anchor in `bias-education.ts academicReference` + Education Room flashcard + chat-coaching context entry in the same commit. The methodology version is now the audit signature — bump it for any structural change to weight calculation; never silently change weights.

- **Pipeline persistence + UI surfacing for R²F signals (locked 2026-04-30 — completes the paper-application sprint #2 + #8):** the validity classification is now PERSISTED in the pipeline at audit-completion time (not just live-computed at render). [/api/analyze/stream](src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts) extends the `judgeOutputs` Json snapshot with `validityClassification` (the full ValidityClassification shape including band + rationale + signals) when each new Analysis row is created. Three downstream surfaces read the persisted band first, with live-compute fallback for legacy analyses: (a) DPR assembler in [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) (DPR cover strip stays in sync with the band the audit was originally scored against); (b) DQI route handlers — [/api/dqi](src/app/api/dqi/route.ts), [/api/v1/dqi](src/app/api/v1/dqi/route.ts), [/api/explainability/[id]](src/app/api/explainability/[analysisId]/route.ts) — read judgeOutputs.validityClassification and pass it to `computeDQI`; (c) live-audit insights endpoint [/api/analysis/[id]/insights](src/app/api/analysis/[id]/insights/route.ts) returns the band with a `validitySource: 'persisted' | 'live'` discriminator so the UI can show provenance ("pipeline-grade" vs "live-computed"). **No schema migration**: the validity classification rides on the existing `Analysis.judgeOutputs` Json column alongside the existing per-judge variance metadata. **UI surface**: new [PaperApplicationsCard](src/components/analysis/PaperApplicationsCard.tsx) renders all three R²F signals (Validity Classification → Reference Class Forecast → Feedback Adequacy) on the document-detail OverviewTab, mounted between RemediationChecklist and RPDPreMortemSuggestionsCard. Reference-class top-3 analogs are clickable links to [/case-studies/{slug}](<src/app/(marketing)/case-studies/[slug]/page.tsx>) so a procurement reader can pivot from the live audit straight to the historical analog. The card mirrors the DPR cover-page strips one-for-one — same colours, same labels, same rationale text — so a buyer who downloads the DPR sees the same content they read on the live audit. **Why this matters**: prior to this lock the validity band on the DPR was computed at PDF-render time and the DQI was computed at scoring time; the two could drift if the documentType changed between scoring and PDF generation. Persisting at audit-completion makes the band immutable for the lifetime of the analysis. The live-audit UI cards close the gap between "audit ran" and "buyer sees the same six R²F blocks the DPR carries" without forcing the DPR PDF download. **Forward-looking rule**: when a new R²F signal ships, follow the same three-tier wire-up — (1) compute + persist in `judgeOutputs` at audit-completion time; (2) DPR + DQI routes read persisted-first with live fallback; (3) UI card on OverviewTab + insights endpoint. Same shape contract every time.

- **Kahneman & Klein 2009 paper-application sprint (locked 2026-04-30 — items 3 of 10 from the first batch):** Three load-bearing operationalisations of the 2009 "Conditions for Intuitive Expertise: A Failure to Disagree" paper, the canonical R²F citation. Shipped together because they answer three procurement-grade questions a Fortune 500 CSO or Pan-African fund partner should be able to ask of an audit ("does this memo's confidence match its evidence?", "did the pre-mortem actually fire prospective hindsight?", "has the author of this memo had enough closed-loop feedback for their experience claim to be calibrated?"). **(#5 — prospective hindsight)** The pre-mortem prompts at [src/lib/agents/prompts.ts](src/lib/agents/prompts.ts) lines 386, 485, and 1075 (STRATEGIC_ANALYSIS_PROMPT, DEEP_ANALYSIS_SUPER_PROMPT, buildNarrativePreMortemPrompt) now enforce the EXACT Klein & Mitchell 1995 / Mitchell-Russo-Pennington 1989 framing: project ONE YEAR INTO THE FUTURE, the plan was implemented as written, the outcome was a TOTAL DISASTER, write the HISTORY of that disaster in past tense ("the failure began when…", "the warning sign everyone missed was…"). NO conditional voice ("might", "could", "if") — the past-tense fait-accompli framing is the load-bearing instruction. The cognitive science: generating an explanation for an outcome framed as ALREADY OCCURRED produces 25-30% more, and substantially higher-quality, failure-cause insights than asking "what could go wrong?" in conditional voice. **(#3 — illusion of validity, DI-B-021)** New bias entry at [src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts](src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts) DI-B-021. Wired through (a) `BiasCategory` union and `BIAS_CATEGORIES` map in [src/types/index.ts](src/types/index.ts), (b) ALIASES in [src/lib/utils/bias-normalize.ts](src/lib/utils/bias-normalize.ts) (so LLM display-name output "Illusion of Validity" / "Illusory Validity" / "Narrative Coherence" / "Confidence by Coherence" all normalize to the canonical key), (c) BIAS_DETECTIVE_PROMPT taxonomy item #21 at `prompts.ts` with rhetorical-certainty signal patterns ("we are certain", "guaranteed", "highly predictable", "clear path to") detected when not backed by external base rates; (d) validity-aware scoring rule (Kahneman & Klein 2009 first condition) — confidence-language penalised harder in low-validity domains (M&A, market entry, long-horizon strategy) than in high-validity ones; (e) four new compound interactions (Illusion of Validity + Overconfidence 1.5×, + Confirmation 1.4×, + Halo 1.3×, + Authority 1.3×); (f) new toxic combination "Coherent Confidence" (Illusion of Validity + Overconfidence + Confirmation/Halo) — the most dangerous pattern in low-validity domains; (g) `forgottenQuestions` taxonomy enum lifted from 31 to 32 biases. **(#6 — feedback adequacy)** New module at [src/lib/learning/feedback-adequacy.ts](src/lib/learning/feedback-adequacy.ts) exporting `getFeedbackAdequacy(prisma, userId, { domainHint })` returning verdict + closedOutcomes + recentClosedOutcomes (18-month window) + daysSinceLastOutcome + meanBrier + domainMatchCount + procurement-grade note. Verdict bands: ≥10 closed outcomes in domain in past 18 months = `adequate`; 3-9 = `sparse`; <3 = `cold_start`; lookup error = `unknown` (transparent fallback, never crashes the DPR path). Wired into the per-analysis DPR data assembler at [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) (running in Promise.all alongside counterfactualImpact + orgCalibration + dataLifecycle); rendered as a dedicated FEEDBACK ADEQUACY · {VERDICT} strip on page 1 of every DPR right below Org Calibration via [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts). Specimen DPR seeded with a sparse-verdict example at [sample-dpr.ts](src/lib/reports/sample-dpr.ts). Cold-start posture is honest: "Per Kahneman & Klein (2009), this is insufficient closed-loop feedback for intuition to be calibrated; treat experience-based claims with the same scrutiny as a cold-start audit." **Education Room flashcards** (advanced tier, kahneman_klein tag): `bias_illusion_of_validity`, `bias_prospective_hindsight`, `bias_feedback_adequacy` in the cognitive_biases deck. **Chat coaching** updated in [founder-context.ts](src/app/api/founder-hub/founder-context.ts) so the AI references all three by name when the founder asks about Kahneman & Klein, R²F operationalisation, overconfident memos, or pre-mortem coaching. **Why this matters**: R²F is the single most defensible positioning asset on the landing page; until 2026-04-30 it was claimed but only partially operationalised. The 2009 paper has at least 10 distinct findings worth implementing — these three are #5 / #3 / #6 of that ranked list (the next 7 are surfaced in the same sprint commit message for sequencing). **Forward-looking rule**: when extending R²F further, reach for the ranked remaining-7 list before adding new R²F surfaces. Adding paper-grounded detectors (vs. heuristic ones) is what makes the moat citable; every new detector should land with the academic anchor in `bias-education.ts academicReference` and an Education Room flashcard in the same commit.
- **Outcome Gate Enforcement (locked 2026-04-26 — Phase 1, the structural fix for the cathedral-of-code trap):** [src/lib/learning/outcome-gate.ts](src/lib/learning/outcome-gate.ts) `checkOutcomeGate(userId, enforce: boolean = false)` now returns `allowed: false` at HARD threshold when `enforce=true`. [src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts](src/app/api/analyze/stream/route.ts) POST looks up `Organization.enforceOutcomeGate` for any org the user belongs to (via TeamMember); if any org has it `true`, the gate enforces. When blocked, returns HTTP 409 with `code: 'OUTCOME_GATE_BLOCKED'` + `pendingCount` + `pendingAnalysisIds` + `level: 'hard'` so the client can route the user to the outcome reporter. Org default = `false` preserves the legacy soft-nudge experience for free / individual / non-design-partner accounts. Design partners flip the flag to `true` as a contractual term of the partnership — the data flywheel becomes contractual, not aspirational. Founder School lesson `es_11` codifies the discovery-call language ("three things are non-negotiable: workflow mapping in this call, audit-before-meeting, outcome-gate enforced at platform level"). **Phase 2 (shipped 2026-04-26 — see Outcome Gate Phase 2 lock above) and Phase 3 (shipped 2026-04-27 — see Outcome Gate Phase 3 lock below)** complete the wiring: the modal now pre-fills the outcome value from auto-detected drafts and routes the submit through `PATCH /api/outcomes/draft action='confirm'` for one-click resolution, with a fallback to manual `POST /api/outcomes` when the user overrides. Migration: `prisma/migrations/20260426170000_add_org_enforce_outcome_gate/migration.sql` adds the `enforceOutcomeGate` column. **Why this matters**: NotebookLM Q6 pre-mortem (saved as note `9a249bd8` in master KB `809f5104`) identified outcome-gate avoidance as the structural failure mode that kills the first paid conversion — the platform now enforces the workflow change so the founder doesn't have to be the heavy in every conversation.

- **Outcome Gate Phase 3 · auto-draft prefill (locked 2026-04-27 — completes the flywheel-friction collapse):** [OutcomeGateModal](src/components/ui/OutcomeGate.tsx) now fetches `/api/outcomes/draft` on mount, builds a `Map<analysisId, DraftOutcome>` filtered to the gate's pending list, and pre-fills the outcome value when the user picks an analysis with a matching draft. UI changes: (a) analysis-list rows render a "Draft ready" pill with Lightbulb icon when a draft exists for that analysis (title attribute carries source + confidence); (b) when an analysis with a draft is selected, an indigo-tinted info pill appears above the outcome buttons showing source name, confidence percent, the first 90 chars of the draft's evidence quote, and "Pre-filled below — confirm to log, or change to override"; (c) the submit button label switches between "Confirm draft outcome" and "Submit & Unlock Analysis" based on whether the user kept or overrode the auto-detected outcome value. **Submission paths**: confirm-path → `PATCH /api/outcomes/draft action='confirm'` (server creates the DecisionOutcome, marks the analysis status, triggers recalibration in one transaction via `confirmDraftOutcome` in [outcome-inference.ts](src/lib/learning/outcome-inference.ts)). Override-path → `POST /api/outcomes` with the user's chosen outcome, plus a fire-and-forget `PATCH /api/outcomes/draft action='dismiss'` to clear the now-stale draft (never block the success path on draft cleanup). **Why this matters**: per CLAUDE.md Unicorn Roadmap pitfalls, Cloverpop's "manual logging adoption trap" is the canonical risk — Outcome Gate enforcement (Phase 1) only compounds the data moat if friction collapses (Phase 3). 3-click → 1-click is the highest-leverage UX move on the moat-data accumulation curve.

- **Demo → account claim flow (locked 2026-04-27 — D9 Tier 2 ship; closes the broken-funnel hole where every wow-moment audit was a dead end):** [`/api/onboarding/claim-demo-analysis`](src/app/api/onboarding/claim-demo-analysis/route.ts) accepts `{ analysisId | documentId }` and atomically transfers `Document.userId` from `DEMO_USER_ID` to the authenticated user via `updateMany` with a predicate (race-safe; two simultaneous claims can't both succeed). 24h window from `Document.uploadedAt` (matches the per-IP demo rate-limit so older audits have already aged out). [/onboarding/claim](src/app/onboarding/claim/page.tsx) is a thin client page that auth-checks (bounces to login with self as redirect), POSTs to the API, and redirects to `/documents/[id]?claimed=true`. Doc detail page reads `?claimed=true` on mount, fires a "Audit claimed from your demo run" success toast, and strips the param from the URL so a refresh doesn't re-fire. **Failure modes**: 401 (unauthed → login redirect); 404 (audit not found); 410 (window expired or already claimed); 409 (lost race); 503 (transient). Each surfaces a specific UI message + retry CTA when retryable. **Why this matters**: per CLAUDE.md the demo runs the real 12-node pipeline at ~£0.40 per audit; without the claim flow, every wow moment was orphaned and the conversion was a cold sign-up to an empty dashboard. Now the visitor lands on THEIR audit at /documents/[id], with the same DQI score and bias list visible.

Empty-state for snapshots with 0 nodes. Mobile-friendly grid layout. - **ICP / positioning constants extraction (locked 2026-04-28 — C1):** [src/lib/constants/icp.ts](src/lib/constants/icp.ts) is the single canonical source for the locked positioning vocabulary that previously lived as prose in three places (founder-context.ts MARKET STRATEGY block, the Expansion line, the FOUNDER NOTES ICP lead, and StartHereTab.tsx Current Positioning Anchor card). Now both consumers read from the canonical source — single edit to icp.ts propagates to chat coaching + founder-facing reference card + any future surface that needs the locked vocabulary. **Forward-looking rule**: when CLAUDE.md "Positioning & Vocabulary" or "ICP — wedge + ceiling" locks change, edit `icp.ts` only; every consumer reads by import.

- **Start Here dynamic map (locked 2026-04-28 — replaces the prior 2-day study plan):** rewrite of [StartHereTab.tsx](src/components/founder-hub/StartHereTab.tsx) plus four new files in [src/components/founder-hub/start-here/](src/components/founder-hub/start-here/). The map is interactive SVG showing every Founder Hub tab as a node grouped by 5 cluster lanes (Start / Product / Go-to-Market / Intelligence / Tools), edges between nodes name real flow handoffs, and 5 journey overlays let the founder pick what they're doing right now (`pitch` / `research` / `outreach` / `reflect` / `product`) and see the recommended sequence highlighted with numbered step badges. **Files**: [founder-hub-map-data.ts](src/components/founder-hub/start-here/founder-hub-map-data.ts) is the SSOT (NODES with payoff + prerequisites + minutes; EDGES naming flow handoffs; JOURNEYS as ordered TabId[] arrays). [JourneyDetailStrip.tsx](src/components/founder-hub/start-here/JourneyDetailStrip.tsx) shows the active journey path as a numbered horizontal step ribbon with "recommended next" highlighted in the journey color. **Persistence preserved**: visited tabs continue to use the legacy `di-study-plan-progress-v1` key so any progress under the old plan carries. Visiting any tab via the map auto-marks visited; manual mark-visited / unvisited button in the hover panel for tabs the founder skim-read elsewhere. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding a new tab, add it to NODES in `founder-hub-map-data.ts` with normalized (x, y) coordinates, prerequisites, minutes, and a payoff line — the map auto-renders it. Renaming a tab → edit only the `label` field; `tabId` is the persistence key. Adding a new journey → push a JOURNEYS entry; the path is an ordered TabId array. Edges are LOGICAL connections (prereq or flow handoff); no decorative lines.

- **F1 platform calibration baseline (locked 2026-04-29):** synthetic Brier-scored calibration derived from running our published DQI methodology over the 143-case library with hindsight neutralised. The deck-grade answer to "show me your outcome calibration" before customer outcomes accumulate; primary defense against Cloverpop's data-advantage attack vector (CLAUDE.md External Attack Vectors). **Source of truth**: [src/lib/learning/platform-baseline.ts](src/lib/learning/platform-baseline.ts) `computePlatformCalibrationBaseline()` — caches at module init, deterministic. `computeBrierFairPredictedDqi(c)` mirrors `computeSyntheticDQI` from `dqi.ts` but neutralises evidenceQuality (the one dimension that peeks at outcome) so predictions are made without hindsight; uses canonical `WEIGHTS` and `OUTCOME_TO_ACTUAL` from existing methodology. Honest seed numbers (computed 2026-04-29): **Brier 0.258 (fair band)** over 143 cases, **52% classification accuracy** at the C/D grade boundary, between CIA-analyst (0.23) and motivated-amateur (0.35) bands per Tetlock anchors. Methodology version `2.0.0-seed`. **Bundle-safe snapshot**: [src/lib/learning/platform-baseline-snapshot.ts](src/lib/learning/platform-baseline-snapshot.ts) — ~200B literals for client surfaces that cannot afford the 750KB case-library import (notably the landing-page hero strip). Drift between snapshot and live computation is caught by [platform-baseline-snapshot.test.ts](src/lib/learning/platform-baseline-snapshot.test.ts). **Surfaces wired**: (1) Every customer DPR via [provenance-record-data.ts](src/lib/reports/provenance-record-data.ts) `buildOrgCalibration` — when an org has no closed outcomes, `OrgCalibrationSummary.source = 'platform_seed'` with `platformSeed` block populated; the DPR generator at [decision-provenance-record-generator.ts](src/lib/reports/decision-provenance-record-generator.ts) renders a "Calibration · platform seed baseline" strip on page 1. (2) Public endpoint at [/api/intelligence/calibration-baseline](src/app/api/intelligence/calibration-baseline/route.ts) — `force-static` with `public, max-age=86400, immutable` since the case library is compile-time-static. (3) [BiasGenomeContributionCard](src/components/insights/BiasGenomeContributionCard.tsx) discovery state — `PlatformBaselineCallout` renders the baseline alongside the "Log an outcome" CTA so a cold-start org sees a Tetlock-anchored number, not just an empty card; the contribution endpoint at [/api/intelligence/bias-genome/contribution](src/app/api/intelligence/bias-genome/contribution/route.ts) carries the baseline in every response. (4) [InvestorMetricsTracker](src/components/founder-hub/path-to-100m/data/investor-metrics.ts) — new "Platform Calibration Credibility" metric (rank 17, presentation discipline, status `on_track`) with the seed Brier as `diCurrent` and per-org Brier as the 12-month target. (5) [/bias-genome](<src/app/(marketing)/bias-genome/page.tsx>) hero meta strip — new "Calibration baseline" Pill alongside Named biases / Case studies / Industries. (6) Landing-page [HeroCredibilityStrip](<src/app/(marketing)/page.tsx>) — extended from 4 to 5 items, new `Activity`-icon row reading "Brier 0.258 calibration · 143 audited corporate decisions." **Investor narrative**: today's seed is the contractual answer until customer outcomes accumulate via Outcome Gate enforcement. Per-org Brier replaces the seed once an org has ≥1 closed outcome; convergence target is the Tetlock superforecaster band (≤ 0.13) as the data flywheel matures. **Forward-looking rule**: when `ALL_CASES` or `computeBrierFairPredictedDqi` changes, regenerate the snapshot literals in `platform-baseline-snapshot.ts` and bump `PLATFORM_BASELINE_SNAPSHOT_COMPUTED_AT`; the drift test will catch divergence in CI. CalibrationChip locked-state integration is a deferred follow-up (would require extending `/api/calibration/profile`, scope creep beyond F1).

- **F2 path-to-100m/data.ts split (locked 2026-04-29):** the monolithic [src/components/founder-hub/path-to-100m/data.ts](src/components/founder-hub/path-to-100m/data.ts) (3,554 lines / 228KB) is split into 12 per-consumer sub-modules under [src/components/founder-hub/path-to-100m/data/](src/components/founder-hub/path-to-100m/data/). Bought ~6 months of build-OOM headroom (the 04-29 webpack-OOM had been surfaced as a current-pace risk; per the build-hang triage, splitting heavy data files via dynamic import was the documented next move when `webpackBuildWorker: false` no longer suffices). **Sub-modules** (each owns one consumer's data + types): `strengths-weaknesses.ts` (StrengthsWeaknessesMatrix), `r2f.ts` (R2FDeepDive), `category-pitch.ts` (CategoryAndPitchLibrary), `role-playbooks.ts` (RoleOutreachPlaybooks — 1,441 lines, the heaviest), `killer-responses.ts` (KillerResponsesPlaybook), `investor-metrics.ts` (InvestorMetricsTracker), `failure-modes.ts` (FailureModesWatchtower), `network-nodes.ts` (WarmIntroNetworkMap), `ninety-day-actions.ts` (NinetyDayActionPlan), `notebook-lm-follow-ups.ts` (NotebookLmFollowUpLab), `silent-objections.ts` (MarketRealityCheck), `simplified-funnel.ts` (SimplifiedThirtyDayFunnel). **`data.ts` is now a thin barrel re-exporter** (~110 lines) keeping backwards-compat for any accidental `from './data'` import; `SECTION_COUNTS` lives in the barrel since it composes counts across all 12 modules. Each consumer is updated to import from its specific sub-module (e.g. `from './data/role-playbooks'`) so a NotebookLM synthesis edit on one section doesn't ripple-rebuild the others. **No external imports exist** outside `path-to-100m/` so no other call sites needed updating. **Forward-looking rule**: when adding new path-to-100m sections, create a new file under `data/` (consumer-aligned), import it in the barrel, and update both the consumer-pointer table in `data.ts` header AND the F4 lock above. NEVER pour new data into the barrel directly — it should stay <120 lines forever.

accepts optional `archetypeId` body field; logs the picked archetype on every generation. **UI** ([ContentGenerator.tsx](src/components/founder-hub/content-studio/ContentGenerator.tsx)): "Voice Archetype" picker row above the topic input with Auto-pick + 6 ranked options + a green-tinted detail card surfacing Hook → Middle → CTA shape + AVOID block + persona target so the founder LEARNS the archetype while using it (Content Studio is also a learning surface, not just a generator). **Smoke test** at [personal-social-system-prompt.test.ts](src/lib/data/personal-social-system-prompt.test.ts) — 19 vitest assertions locking composer behavior, keyword routing, banned-vocab presence, voice/META block presence, truncation. **Education Room deck** added: `personal_social_archetypes` deck (8 cards: 6 archetypes + the empathic-mode-first cold-context discipline + the Polite-but-Brutal Pragmatist META rule) so the founder can drill the patterns himself before writing without AI assist. **Sister-route audit also shipped**: [WeeklyBrief route](src/app/api/founder-hub/content/weekly-brief/route.ts) had a stale "20-bias taxonomy" string (count drift; Sources `HISTORICAL_CASE_COUNT` from canonical so the case count never drifts. **Forward-looking rule**: when the v3.3 plan file changes (signing tests fire / Sankore activates / new investor probe surfaces in conversation), update the card content in StartHereTab in the same commit.

- **Discovery + tailored-pitch hybrid toolkit (locked 2026-05-01 — v3.3 §7 ship):** the most-load-bearing pre-event reference for the next 90 days of in-person events + warm-intro conversations. Three artefacts ship together: (a) [src/lib/data/discovery-pitch-toolkit.ts](src/lib/data/discovery-pitch-toolkit.ts) — typed source-of-truth exporting `DISCOVERY_QUESTIONS` (4 verbatim Mom-Test questions with watch-for cues), `DEFLECTION_SCRIPT` ("I'm researching whether a problem in strategic decision-making is real..."), `PERSONA_OPENERS` (4: cso / ma_corpdev / fund_partner / gc_compliance — fund_partner carries the never-name-Sankore discipline note), `PITCH_TRIGGERS` (8 if-revealed-X-then-pitch-Y triggers covering four-tool-graveyard / specific-blind-spot / audit-committee-Q&A / cross-border-regulatory / never-paid / paying-Cloverpop / AI-assisted-memos / agent-generated-memos), `DISCOVERY_DISCIPLINE_RULES`, `FOLLOWUP_EMAIL_TEMPLATE`, `WHAT_30_CONVERSATIONS_PRODUCE`. (b) [DiscoveryPitchPanel](src/components/founder-hub/sales/DiscoveryPitchPanel.tsx) — interactive component mounted at the TOP of [SalesToolkitTab](src/components/founder-hub/SalesToolkitTab.tsx) (highest visibility); collapsible pitch-trigger cards keyed off discovery signals; persona toggle. (c) [docs/discovery-card-v1.md](docs/discovery-card-v1.md) — printable phone-readable Markdown reference for back-of-Uber pre-event recall. **Why hybrid not pure Mom Test**: founder's burn-rate constraint forces the trade. Pure 30-conversation discovery discipline maximises data quality but burns runway; hybrid preserves data quality (discovery FIRST within each conversation, before any pitch — all 4 Qs in order) while capturing conversion (after Q4, pivot with "Based on what you said about [their pain in their words], I think I have something you should see" + pitch tailored to the signal). Cost: ~10% data-quality erosion as early-conversation pitches anchor framing. Benefit: revenue compounds while discovery accumulates. **Forward-looking rule**: edit the typed exports in `discovery-pitch-toolkit.ts` only; the panel + the Markdown card both regenerate from it. Pattern-match across 10+ conversations before declaring the hybrid working; if the pattern doesn't converge on a coherent 5-word pain language + price band, the wedge is wrong, not the questions.

The migration is in `prisma/migrations/`; founder runs `npx prisma migrate deploy` against production manually per CLAUDE.md "Modifying the analysis pipeline" rule. **Forward-looking rule**: when fixing a Prisma field name typo, always (1) write the migration as RENAME COLUMN (preserves data), (2) verify single sed pattern handles all CamelCase variants, (3) regenerate Prisma client (`npx prisma generate`) and run `tsc --noEmit` BEFORE committing — the type system catches any missed callers loudly.

### Visualization Components (light-theme audit rule)

- Visualization cards (`ToxicCombinationCard`, `RiskHeatMap`, `GraphDetailPanel`, `DecisionTimeline`, `StakeholderMap`) keep dark-theme Tailwind classes **inside** their colored severity wrappers (`bg-red-950/40`, `bg-amber-950/20`) — that is correct, the interior is dark.
- The audit rule: check only the **outermost** heading and elements that sit directly on the page surface. Any `text-white` on a standalone heading outside a dark wrapper is a bug. Interiors on red/amber/yellow severity cards can stay dark.
- Same rule for `ActivityFeed` — rendered inside a platform `.card` (light), so its row content uses `var(--text-primary/secondary/muted)`, not `text-white` or `text-gray-400`.

### DQI Grade Boundaries (locked)

- Canonical grade scale: A 85+, B 70+, C 55+, D 40+, F 0+ — matches `src/lib/scoring/dqi.ts` → `GRADE_THRESHOLDS`.
- The JSDoc at the top of `dqi.ts` is the external reference. **Update both** the comment AND `GRADE_THRESHOLDS` when changing boundaries, or the published contract drifts from runtime.

### Sparkles Icon Discipline (locked 2026-04-26)

`Sparkles` from `lucide-react` is the universal "built with AI" tell — banned on every category pill, badge, and eyebrow chip on every marketing surface and on every public share view. Audit this rule whenever adding a new badge or pill on `(marketing)/**` or `src/app/shared/**`. The 2026-04-26 sweep stripped Sparkles from `FeaturedDeepCases.tsx`, `CaseStudyGrid.tsx`, `case-studies/sample/[slug]/page.tsx`, and two sites in `shared/[token]/page.tsx`. Two exceptions stay legal: (1) the AI Copilot surface chrome at `/dashboard/ask` (Sparkles next to the chat composer reads as "this is an AI surface" and is on-brand for the assistant pattern), (2) the Free-tier "N free this month" reassurance chip on `/dashboard` (platform chrome, not marketing). Every other Sparkles needs a justification or it gets cut.

### NUDGE_TYPE_LABELS Discipline (locked 2026-04-26, hardened 2026-04-27)

Every new `Nudge.nudgeType` enum value MUST land with a label in [src/lib/constants/human-audit.ts](src/lib/constants/human-audit.ts) `NUDGE_TYPE_LABELS` IN THE SAME COMMIT. The 2026-04-26 audit caught `bias_comment_mention` (shipped commit bf6b038, ~Apr 22) had no label entry — every @mention nudge in the dashboard `NudgeWidget` and `NudgesPageContent` rendered the raw enum string instead of "Comment Mention" for ~4 days. The render fallback (`|| nudge.nudgeType`) hides this from compile-time checks; the test you want is "manually create a Nudge with the new type and verify the label renders." Before adding a new nudgeType: search `NUDGE_TYPE_LABELS` and add the label. The 2026-04-27 audit caught FIVE more missing entries: `toxic_combination`, `pre_decision_coaching`, `document_access_granted`, `bias_task_assigned`, `playbook_followup`. These had been shipping silently for weeks across 7+ creator sites. All five added in the same sweep; a comment block above the labels map now records the discipline so future sessions search `nudgeType:` first. **Defensive move**: when adding a NEW nudge creation site, run `rg -nP "nudgeType:\s*['\"][a-z_]+['\"]" src/ --type=ts | rg -v "test\.ts"` and verify every distinct value appears in `NUDGE_TYPE_LABELS`. If you find a new value that's used in two places but missing from labels, that's a bug — not a feature request.

### Onborda Tour Registration Discipline (locked 2026-04-26)

Every role added to `Role = 'cso' | 'ma' | 'bizops' | 'pe_vc' | 'other'` MUST also be registered in the Onborda steps array at [OnboardingTour.tsx](src/components/onboarding/OnboardingTour.tsx) `OnboardingTourProvider`. Defining `TOUR_STEPS_BY_ROLE.<role>` and `TOUR_NAME_BY_ROLE.<role>` is NOT enough — Onborda needs the explicit `{ tour: 'dashboard-tour-<role>', steps: TOUR_STEPS_BY_ROLE.<role> }` entry or the tour silently never fires (users fall through to the default 'dashboard-tour'). The 2026-04-26 audit caught pe_vc was missing the registration even though everything else cascaded correctly — runtime bug, no compile error.

### Stripe / Commerce Dedup Discipline (locked 2026-04-26, extended 2026-04-27)

Any `findFirst` query that gates a Stripe checkout (active-purchase dedup, subscription state, idempotency check) MUST fail-closed on query failure, not silently fall through to a "looks like nothing exists" branch. The 2026-04-26 audit caught `src/app/api/stripe/deal-audit/route.ts:61` was wrapped in `.catch(() => null)`, which would have let the route create a NEW Stripe checkout session for an already-purchased deal on a transient DB error → double-charge the customer. The fix pattern: explicit `try/catch` around the dedup, log the error, return a 503 "Could not verify purchase state. Please retry." Cron-side dedups (e.g. `usage-nudges/route.ts` NotificationLog idempotency check) follow the same rule for the same reason — silent fallthrough → duplicate-send. The fail-closed rule applies wherever the next action is irreversible (charge, send email, post Slack, write blockchain). For pure UI fetches the silent-warn pattern is still acceptable. The 2026-04-27 audit applied the same rule to `src/app/api/stripe/checkout/route.ts:42` — subscription lookup before customer-reuse was `.catch(() => null)`, which on a transient DB failure would silently skip the customer-reuse path and create a duplicate Stripe customer record. Different consequence than deal-audit (duplicate customer, not double-charge) but same fail-open class. Hardened to fail-closed with 503 retry-please. **Forward-looking rule**: every NEW route that contains a Stripe `checkout.sessions.create` call must have its preceding lookup queries fail-closed in the same commit. No silent catches between auth and Stripe.

### Bias Taxonomy

- **22 biases with stable taxonomy IDs: DI-B-001 through DI-B-022** (defined in `src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts`). **DI-B-021 (illusion_of_validity)** and **DI-B-022 (inside_view_dominance)** were added 2026-04-30 as part of the Kahneman & Klein 2009 paper-application sprint (anchored on the 2009 paper for DI-B-021 and Kahneman & Lovallo 2003 "Delusions of Success" HBR for DI-B-022).
- These IDs are permanent and published at `/taxonomy`. Never renumber or reassign them.
- Biases are referenced by snake_case string keys (e.g., `confirmation_bias`, `anchoring_bias`, `illusion_of_validity`, `inside_view_dominance`).
- **Adding a new bias is a load-bearing cascade.** When DI-B-023 lands, every one of these surfaces must update in the same commit: (1) `BiasCategory` union in `src/types/index.ts`, (2) `BIAS_CATEGORIES` map in the same file, (3) `BIAS_EDUCATION` entry in `src/lib/constants/bias-education.ts`, (4) `ALIASES` map in `src/lib/utils/bias-normalize.ts` so LLM display-name output normalizes back, (5) `BIAS_DETECTIVE_PROMPT` taxonomy enumeration + (6) any compound interactions + (7) any toxic combinations in `src/lib/agents/prompts.ts`, (8) the `forgottenQuestions` taxonomy enum count in the same file (currently "33-bias taxonomy"), (9) Education Room flashcard in `src/components/founder-hub/education/education-room-data.ts` cognitive_biases deck, (10) this CLAUDE.md count + ID range. The discriminated-union BiasCategory will fail compilation loudly if any consumer is missed — trust the type system but do the cascade in one PR.

### Plan Limits & Billing

- Free tier: 4 analyses/month (defined in `src/lib/stripe.ts` → `PLANS.free.analysesPerMonth`)
- Limit enforced by `checkAnalysisLimit()` in `src/lib/utils/plan-limits.ts`
- Stripe price IDs may not be configured yet. Upgrade buttons must fall back gracefully to `/#pricing` when `PLANS.pro.priceId` is empty.
- **Admin full-access bypass.** Supabase user IDs listed in `ADMIN_USER_IDS` (Vercel env var, comma-separated) resolve to the `enterprise` plan in `getUserPlan()` / `getOrgPlan()` / `/api/billing` — no Stripe subscription needed. Intended for founder dogfooding and end-to-end testing. Bootstrap: set `ADMIN_EMAILS` first, deploy, visit `/api/admin/whoami` to discover your Supabase UUID, then paste into `ADMIN_USER_IDS` and redeploy. Helper: `isAdminUserId(userId)` in `src/lib/utils/admin.ts`.

### Integrations

- **Slack:** 7 slash commands, thread monitoring, auto-creates CopilotSession + DecisionRoom after audits. Handler in `src/app/api/integrations/slack/events/route.ts`.
- **Google Drive:** OAuth + Changes API polling via cron. Dedup by `sourceRef` (Google file ID). Detects updated files by content hash comparison. 24h cooldown between re-analyses.
- **Email:** Unique address per user (`analyze+{token}@in.decision-intel.com`). Token-based auth.

## When to Push Back

Claude should push back on requests that:

1. **Add new top-level routes** — the sidebar already has 10 items and 25+ dashboard routes. Consolidate instead.
2. **Add features before the core flow is polished** — upload → analyze → review → track outcomes is the only flow that matters for pilot users.
3. **Skip error handling or schema drift protection** — every Prisma query in an API route needs a try-catch with P2021/P2022 fallback.
4. **Use hardcoded dark-mode colors** — always use CSS variables.
5. **Create duplicate utility functions** — check `src/lib/utils/` first. Especially `safe-compare.ts`, `cache.ts`, `rate-limit.ts`, `encryption.ts`.
6. **Make changes that break the build without testing** — run `npx tsc --noEmit` after significant changes.
7. **Add scope beyond what was asked** — the founder is in refinement phase. Don't add docstrings, comments, or refactoring that wasn't requested. **Exception**: when the request IS explicitly scoped as planned/Tier-N work (boil-the-ocean rule above), depth within the approved scope is required, not creep. The line is whether the deepening serves the approved item or wanders into adjacent surfaces.

## When to Ask Questions

Claude should ask the founder before:

1. **Creating new database models or fields** — schema changes require migrations and affect production.
2. **Modifying the analysis pipeline** (`src/lib/agents/`) — this is the core product. Even small changes can affect DQI scores across all users.
3. **Changing pricing, plan limits, or billing logic** — revenue-sensitive.
4. **Deleting any route or component** — may have external links, bookmarks, or Slack deep links pointing to it.
5. **Making changes visible to end users** (copy, labels, flow changes) — the founder has specific positioning and language preferences.

**Proactive-surfacing rule (locked 2026-05-09 evening — supersedes the default-skip pattern).** "Ask first" does NOT mean "default skip." When working on a non-trivial ship, Claude should ACTIVELY scan for high-leverage improvements in the pipeline / DQI / graph / Prisma / scoring engine that would deepen the build, then PROACTIVELY surface them to the founder with: (a) the specific change, (b) why it's high-leverage (load-bearing for what specifically — demo, procurement defensibility, future-proofing, etc.), (c) cost estimate (LOC + complexity), (d) risk assessment (what existing behaviour might shift), (e) clear recommendation. The founder decides; Claude then ships the deep version. Pre-shrinking by silently classifying improvements as "out of scope per the pipeline rule" burns the founder's leverage. The rule's true intent is "don't ship pipeline changes silently" — not "avoid pipeline work." Forward-looking: at the end of every multi-commit ship, run a brief "what did I deliberately skip touching the hard layers, and was that the right call" audit; surface the items where the answer is "no, this should ship." See "Velocity & Scope Discipline" lock above for the parent calibration.

## Build Hang Triage (READ THIS BEFORE TOUCHING THE BUILD)

Vercel build hangs cost ~$0 in money but ~45 minutes per attempt. The 2026-04-22 incident burned 11 hours and 30+ deploys because the right fix was found at hour 0, reverted at hour 1, then re-discovered at hour 11. Don't repeat that loop. The diagnostic chain below is the load-bearing artifact from that incident.

**Step 1 — locate the hang.** Pull the Vercel build logs and find the LAST log line before silence. Three known patterns:

| Last visible log line                                    | Cause                                                                                                                                                                                           | Fix                                                                                                |
| -------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `Successfully uploaded source maps to Sentry`            | [getsentry/sentry-javascript#17511](https://github.com/getsentry/sentry-javascript/issues/17511) — webpack plugin leaks undici sockets after upload, `runAfterProductionCompile` never resolves | `sourcemaps: { disable: true }` in `withSentryConfig` options. Already applied — do NOT revert it. |
| `Creating an optimized production build ...` (Turbopack) | Some Turbopack-only stall in this codebase. Not yet isolated.                                                                                                                                   | Stay on `next build --webpack`. The `--webpack` flag in `package.json:7` is load-bearing.          |
| `Creating an optimized production build ...` (webpack)   | Likely SWC infinite-loop on inline `<style>{`@media...`}</style>` blocks if `compiler.styledJsx: false` is missing                                                                              | Confirm `compiler: { styledJsx: false }` is in `next.config.ts`.                                   |

**Step 2 — reproduce locally before pushing any fix.** `npm run build` reproduces most build issues in 3-4 minutes. A failing local build is 10× cheaper to debug than a failing Vercel deploy. If it passes locally but fails on Vercel, the bug is environment-specific (network, container resource limits, Linux SWC binary differences) — and that itself narrows the search.

**Step 3 — bisect, don't theorize.** When N commits land between the last-green and the first-red, run `git bisect` against `npm run build`. The 2026-04-22 incident had 15 commits + ~5,000 LOC between green and red — bisection would have isolated the trigger in 4 build runs (~15 min) instead of 11 hours of theory-chasing.

**Things that have been ruled out as primary causes** (don't re-investigate without new evidence):

- Google Fonts fetch hang — fonts are now `@fontsource` local packages.
- `next/font/google` — removed.
- Turbopack font fetcher Rust HTTP path — fonts are local, the path doesn't fire.
- Sentry plugin telemetry — `telemetry: false` in `withSentryConfig`.
- Sentry source-map upload — DISABLED in `withSentryConfig`. **This is the load-bearing fix; do not revert.** Source maps will be uploaded post-deploy via the separate `npm run sentry:upload-sourcemaps` step (see Environment Variables → `SENTRY_AUTH_TOKEN`).
- Edge runtime on `app/opengraph-image.tsx` — file deleted; static OG image lives in `public/` instead.
- Heap exhaustion — `--max-old-space-size=7168` in NODE_OPTIONS gives webpack ~7 GB on Vercel's 8 GB build container; the pre-build tsc runs at `--max-old-space-size=3584` (~3.5 GB) in its own process, exits, then webpack starts.
- TypeScript errors — `npx tsc --noEmit` now runs clean; type-check phase no longer hangs silently on errors.
- **Stacked heap from two concurrent TS checks** (2026-04-23, deploy 4Sz9sqTpr, exit 137 after 6 min in "Running TypeScript..."). Next.js runs its own in-process TS check AFTER webpack compile finishes; combined with webpack's own heap it blew past 8 GB. Fix shipped: `typescript: { ignoreBuildErrors: true }` in next.config.ts, plus an explicit `NODE_OPTIONS='--max-old-space-size=3584' npx tsc --noEmit` step in the build script that runs **before** `next build`. The external tsc runs in its own process (~3 GB peak, then exits), then webpack runs at ~5 GB peak — never overlapping. Do NOT flip `ignoreBuildErrors` off without also removing the explicit tsc step, or type-checking gets silently skipped.
- **Webpack OOM at 6 GB heap** (2026-04-25, exit 137 during "Creating an optimized production build"). Codebase grew large enough that webpack's compile pass exceeded 6 GB even after the tsc step had freed its memory. Two-line fix shipped: (a) bumped webpack heap to 7168 (giving webpack ~7 GB on the 8 GB container, leaving ~1 GB for parent Node + container overhead) and dropped tsc heap to 3584 to phase the pressure cleanly, (b) enabled `experimental.webpackMemoryOptimizations: true` in next.config.ts — Next 16's built-in webpack memory optimization that drops a few non-essential webpack passes (unused-variable analysis tuning, some source-map auxiliary work) to keep peak memory under the 8 GB ceiling. No runtime impact; only changes how webpack does its bookkeeping during compile. Do NOT raise the heap above 7168 — that pushes the process into the parent-Node + container-overhead window and the SIGKILL fires.
- **Webpack OOM AGAIN at 7 GB heap** (2026-04-29, exit 137 during `next build --webpack` — even with `webpackMemoryOptimizations: true` already on). Codebase grew across the prior 7 days (Sparring Room v3 ~1700 lines, Education Room ~120 cards, Path-to-100M tab + ~3000-line data file, Closing Lab + Brinkmanship + Strategic Thinking sales-toolkit additions, founder-school lesson + visualization growth, the case-count drift refactor touching ~30 files). Fix: added `experimental.webpackBuildWorker: false` per the previously-documented next-OOM-move. Next 16+ runs webpack in a worker by default; disabling it can PARADOXICALLY reduce peak memory because the worker duplicates internal state that already lives in the parent process. **Did NOT switch to Turbopack** — per CLAUDE.md Build Hang Triage `--webpack` flag is load-bearing, and Turbopack stalled in this codebase on 2026-04-22 ("Creating an optimized production build ..." never recovered). Treat Turbopack as the experimental fallback ONLY if this commit's fix also OOMs. **If the 2026-04-29 fix also OOMs**, the next options are: (a) split heavy data files via dynamic import — best candidates: `src/lib/data/founder-school/lessons.ts` (~16K lines), `src/lib/data/founder-school/visualizations.ts` (~1300 lines), `src/components/founder-hub/path-to-100m/data.ts` (~3000 lines), `src/components/founder-hub/education/education-room-data.ts` (~1700 lines) — wrap consumers in dynamic({ loading: ... }) so these don't hit the main bundle, (b) try Turbopack again if Next 16.x has improved the codebase compatibility (NB: this requires removing the `--webpack` flag from package.json :: scripts.build and likely fixing some inline-style edge cases SWC/Turbopack handles differently from webpack), (c) bump Vercel build-machine to a larger instance (Pro tier).
- **Webpack OOM (third) at 7 GB heap** (2026-05-06, exit 137 — even with all prior fixes already in place: heap 7168 + `webpackBuildWorker: false` + `webpackMemoryOptimizations: true`). Build log named the culprit explicitly — webpack's `PackFileCacheStrategy` was serialising 700+ MB cache packs (`.next/cache/webpack/server-production/1.pack` at 702 MB, `43.pack` at 428 MB, `index.pack` at 448 MB) and holding them in memory during serialisation, pushing peak heap past the 8 GB container ceiling. **Fix shipped**: added a `webpack(config, { dev })` callback in `next.config.ts` that sets `config.cache = false` for production builds. Vercel runs each deploy on a fresh container, so the on-disk cache hit rate is near-zero anyway — the disk packs were compute that never paid back. Trade-off: cold first-build locally on every restart (~3 min addition) but no impact on Vercel CI behaviour. Memory-cache alternative was rejected — webpack's memory cache also holds modules for the duration of the build, which at the codebase's current size also OOMs; only `cache: false` is stable. **If the 2026-05-06 fix also OOMs** (which would mean webpack's compile-only memory has crossed 7 GB without any cache contribution), the next options remain: (a) heavy-data-file dynamic-import splits per the 2026-04-29 list, (b) Turbopack retry, (c) Pro-tier larger build container.

**The load-bearing config — do not change without a passing build to prove the alternative works:**

- `package.json:7` build script: chain is `validate-deploy-env && prisma-migrate-safe && seed-business-data && tsc --noEmit && next build --webpack && upload-sourcemaps`. The external `tsc --noEmit` step is load-bearing per the 2026-04-23 stacked-heap fix. `seed-business-data.mjs` (added 2026-04-24) runs version-controlled pilot-data seeds (currently just Sankore) after migrations; it is create-only by default so UI edits to `founderNotes` are never clobbered, and it NEVER fails the build — DB-unreachable or seed-script errors log a warning and exit 0. Business data is not build-artifact-critical; the 11-hr build-hang postmortem's lesson is "don't let optional steps block the deploy."
- `next.config.ts` Sentry options: `sourcemaps: { disable: true }`
- `next.config.ts` compiler: `compiler: { styledJsx: false }`
- `next.config.ts` typescript: `{ ignoreBuildErrors: true }` — paired with the external tsc step above. Flip one, flip both.
- `NODE_OPTIONS='--max-old-space-size=7168'` on `next build`; `--max-old-space-size=3584` on the pre-build `tsc --noEmit` (raised webpack / lowered tsc 2026-04-25 to fix webpack OOM at the previous 6144 ceiling).
- `next.config.ts` `experimental.webpackMemoryOptimizations: true` (added 2026-04-25 alongside the heap rebalance — Next 16's built-in webpack memory optimization).

## Session Workflow

Claude Code sessions should follow this pattern for best results:

0. **Read TODO.md first.** Check `TODO.md` at the start of every session for known bugs, active priorities, and pending tasks. Update it as tasks are completed or new issues are discovered.
1. **Start small.** One focused task per session beats a mega-batch across 20 files. Context quality degrades past ~15 file modifications.
2. **Build-check before pushing.** Always run `npx tsc --noEmit` (fast, type-errors only) or `npm run build` (full build) before committing. The founder doesn't run builds locally — Claude IS the local build check.
3. **Commit after each logical unit.** Don't batch 12 changes into one commit. Ship fix → commit → next fix → commit.
4. **Don't rediscover — read CLAUDE.md.** The conventions here (CSS variables, `uploadedAt` not `createdAt`, `safeCompare` import) have all been learned the hard way.
5. **Pre-commit hook note:** There is a Gemini AI audit hook in `.husky/pre-commit` that runs `npm run audit:ai`. It can be slow. If it blocks and the changes are reviewed, use `--no-verify`.
6. **Keep CLAUDE.md current — proactively, not at session end.** Whenever a change introduces a new convention, renames a field, adds a critical file, changes a workflow pattern, or discovers a gotcha that cost time — update CLAUDE.md **in the same commit** as that change. Don't wait until the session ends. Don't ask permission. Just include the CLAUDE.md edit alongside the code change. Examples: adding a new Prisma field → update the Database section. Creating a new shared utility → add it to Key Files. Discovering a build error caused by a naming convention → add it to Critical Conventions. The goal is that the next session (which has zero memory of this one) starts with every lesson already learned.

## Debugging Discipline (locked 2026-04-22 after the 11-hour build-hang incident)

These five rules exist because the 2026-04-22 build-hang debug burned 11 hours and 30+ deploys re-discovering a fix that had already been found and wrongly reverted at hour 1. They are not optional.

1. **A working fix is not reverted without a NEW failing test that proves it wasn't the cause.** "It used to work without this" / "the old log shows this never fired" / "this can't be the cause because X" are guesses, not evidence. If a commit makes the build go green, the burden of proof is on the revert, not the keep. The 2026-04-22 incident's killer mistake was `c6af4ab` reverting `c1540a1`'s `sourcemaps: { disable: true }` on exactly this kind of "it used to work" reasoning.

2. **Bisect before theorize.** When N commits land between the last-green and the first-red, `git bisect run npm run build` is faster than any theory. Three builds (~12 min) beats three hours of reading code.

3. **Reproduce locally before pushing.** Each Vercel deploy attempt is 8-45 minutes. `npm run build` reproduces most issues in 3-4 minutes. Local first; push only after the local repro confirms the fix.

4. **Memory and commit messages record evidence + uncertainty, not conclusions.** Banned phrasings: "THE ACTUAL BUG", "definitively the culprit", "real root cause", "this is the fix". Every one of these in the 2026-04-22 commit history was followed by another red build. Use instead: "tried X, build now hangs at Y instead of Z" / "X eliminates the hang in deploy ABC123 — keeping unless disproved by a new failing case." The next session reads commit messages as ground truth — don't lie to it.

5. **Don't accumulate scaffolding without removing on disproof.** Each rejected hypothesis leaves debt: env vars, scripts, NODE_OPTIONS flags, config keys. When a hypothesis is disproved, delete its scaffolding in the same commit as the disproof, or document it as deliberately-kept-for-X with a date. The current build script still carries `patch-http-timeout.mjs` from a Google Fonts theory that's been irrelevant since fonts went local — don't let that pile grow.

## Sub-Agent Strategy

Use the right model for the right job. Never use Opus for tasks Haiku can handle.

**Exploration (Haiku, 3 in parallel):**
Use Haiku sub-agents for all read-only codebase exploration — file reading, grep searches, structure mapping, "find all places X is used" pattern analysis. Haiku reads files and reports back just as accurately as Opus. Launch up to 3 in parallel for maximum speed. Always specify `model: "haiku"` and `subagent_type: "Explore"` for these.

**Planning (Opus, main thread):**
Do implementation planning in the main conversation thread, not in sub-agents. The main thread has the full conversation context, user intent, and prior decisions. Delegating planning to a sub-agent loses this context and produces generic results. The one exception: use a Plan sub-agent (Opus) for very complex multi-file architectural decisions where a fresh perspective helps.

**Implementation (Opus, main thread, direct edits):**
Never delegate code implementation to sub-agents. Always edit files directly in the main thread. The main thread has the conversation history, knows what was tried, and can make judgment calls. Sub-agents writing code produce lower-quality output because they lack this context.

**Verification (Sonnet or direct Bash):**
For mechanical checks — type-checking, test runs, build verification, counting occurrences — use direct Bash commands (preferred) or Sonnet sub-agents if parallel checking is needed. These tasks don't need Opus-level reasoning.
